F3 Diagnostic Functions Manual


  Diagnostic Functions Links

The following are links to the specifications of the diagnostic functions supported by the
diagnostic firmware.  If a supported function has not yet been documented, then it will be
listed but no link will be available.  The documentation of the diagnostic firmware's SDBP
interface will grow rapidly to include more  specifications of supported functions in the
coming weeks.

  Control Functions


0001: Enable Online Mode Requests

0002: Disable Online Mode Requests

0003: Enable Diagnostic Mode Requests

0004: Disable Diagnostic Mode Requests

0005: Abort Diagnostic Activity

  Diagnostic Functions Specifications




 Abort Diagnostic Activity


  Description:
    This control mode diagnostic function attempts to abort any diagnostic that is
    currently being executed.

  Diagnostic Function Block:


  

   Name
   Byte
Index		
   Value
   Description
  

  

   

SdbpHeader (Structure, Length=8)

SdbpHeader is Seagate Diagnostic Bridge / Router Protocol (SDBP) packet header.
    

  

  

   

FromPort
   

   
0
   
   
0x07
   
   
FromPort is the SDBP Port on the host or drive where this packet came from.
   
  

  

   
1
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   

ToPort
   

   
2
   
   
0x07
   
   
ToPort is the SDBP Port on the host or drive where this packet is going.
   
  

  

   
3
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   

Length
   

   
4
   
   
0x0C
   
   
Length is the length in bytes of the packet not including the SDBP packet header.
   
  

  

   
5
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   
6
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   
7
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   

Dfb (Structure, Length=4)

Dfb is a generic Diagnostic Function Block (DFB).
    

  

  

   

Header (Structure, Length=4)

Header is the extrinsic Diagnostic Function Block (DFB) header.
    

  

  

   

FunctionId
   

   
8
   
   
0x05
   
   
FunctionId is the ID of the diagnostic function to be executed.
   
  

  

   
9
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   

RevisionId
   

   
10
   
   
0x01
   
   
RevisionId is the revision of the parameters for the diagnostic function.
   
  

  

   
11
   
   
0x00
   
  




  Diagnostic Status Block:


  

   Name
   Byte
Index		
   Value
   Description
  

  

   

SdbpHeader (Structure, Length=8)

SdbpHeader is Seagate Diagnostic Bridge / Router Protocol (SDBP) packet header.
    

  

  

   

FromPort
   

   
0
   
   
0x07
   
   
FromPort is the SDBP Port on the host or drive where this packet came from.
   
  

  

   
1
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   

ToPort
   

   
2
   
   
0x07
   
   
ToPort is the SDBP Port on the host or drive where this packet is going.
   
  

  

   
3
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   

Length
   

   
4
   
   
0x10
   
   
Length is the length in bytes of the packet not including the SDBP packet header.
   
  

  

   
5
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   
6
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   
7
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   

Dsb (Structure, Length=8)

Dsb is a generic Diagnostic Status Block (DSB).
    

  

  

   

Header (Structure, Length=8)

Header is the extrinsic Diagnostic Status Block (DSB) header.
    

  

  

   

DataTypeId
   

   
8
   
   
0x01
   
   
DataTypeId specifies the type of data being returned.  The allowed values are defined by

the "diag_data_type_id" enumeration.
   		
  

  

   
9
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   

RevisionId
   

   
10
   
   
0x01
   
   
RevisionId specifies the revision of the diagnostic data returned by the diagnostic

function.
   		
  

  

   
11
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   

Error
   

   
12
   
   
 
   
   
Error contains the Diagnostic Test Service error code.  See the link below for all the

supported error codes.

Diagnostic Error Codes

14

 Buffer DLL Tune


  Description:
    This diagnostic mode function exercises the Buffer DLL Tune diagnostic.

  Diagnostic Function Block:


  

   Name
   Byte
Index		
   Value
   Description
  

  

   

SdbpHeader (Structure, Length=8)

SdbpHeader is Seagate Diagnostic Bridge / Router Protocol (SDBP) packet header.
    

  

  

   

FromPort
   

   
0
   
   
0x07
   
   
FromPort is the SDBP Port on the host or drive where this packet came from.
   
  

  

   
1
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   

ToPort
   

   
2
   
   
0x07
   
   
ToPort is the SDBP Port on the host or drive where this packet is going.
   
  

  

   
3
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   

Length
   

   
4
   
   
0x1C
   
   
Length is the length in bytes of the packet not including the SDBP packet header.
   
  

  

   
5
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   
6
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   
7
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   

Dfb (Structure, Length=12)

Dfb is the Diagnostic Function Block (DFB) for the Buffer DLL Tune diagnostic.
    

  

  

   

Header (Structure, Length=4)

Header is the Diagnostic Function Block (DFB) header.
    

  

  

   

FunctionId
   

   
8
   
   
0x0C
   
   
FunctionId is the ID of the diagnostic function to be executed.
   
  

  

   
9
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   

RevisionId
   

   
10
   
   
0x01
   
   
RevisionId is the revision of the parameters for the diagnostic function.
   
  

  

   
11
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   

Action
   

   
12
   
   
 
   
   
Action indicates what this command is to do.


0: Display value currently in bypass register

1: not used

2: Enable periodic compensation.

3: Disable periodic compensation.

4: Enable display of compensation.

5: Disable display of compensation.

9: Set new bypass value to specified value.

   		
  

  

   
13
   
   
 
   
  

  

   
14
   
   
 
   
  

  

   
15
   
   
 
   
  

  

   

NewDllValue
   

   
16
   
   
 
   
   
NewDllValue is the value to load into the DLL bypass.
   
  

  

   
17
   
   
 
   
  

  

   
18
   
   
 
   
  

  

   
19
   
   
 
   
  




  Diagnostic Status Block:


  

   Name

   Value
   Description

 Collect PES


  Description:
    This diagnostic mode diagnostic function collects on-track PES data.  The data returned
    by this function will be an array of 16-bit values representing PES in Q12 format (i.e.
    4096 counts per track).

  Diagnostic Function Block:


  

   Name
   Byte
Index		
   Value
   Description
  

  

   

SdbpHeader (Structure, Length=8)

SdbpHeader is Seagate Diagnostic Bridge / Router Protocol (SDBP) packet header.
    

  

  

   

FromPort
   

   
0
   
   
0x07
   
   
FromPort is the SDBP Port on the host or drive where this packet came from.
   
  

  

   
1
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   

ToPort
   

   
2
   
   
0x07
   
   
ToPort is the SDBP Port on the host or drive where this packet is going.
   
  

  

   
3
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   

Length
   

   
4
   
   
0x06
   
   
Length is the length in bytes of the packet not including the SDBP packet header.
   
  

  

   
5
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   
6
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   
7
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   

Dfb (Structure, Length=6)

Dfb is the Diagnostic Function Block (DFB) for the Collect PES diagnostic.
    

  

  

   

Header (Structure, Length=4)

Header is the Diagnostic Status Block (DSB) header.
    

  

  

   

FunctionId
   

   
8
   
   
0x6B
   
   
FunctionId is the ID of the diagnostic function to be executed.
   
  

  

   
9
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   

RevisionId
   

   
10
   
   
0x01
   
   
RevisionId is the revision of the parameters for the diagnostic function.
   
  

  

   
11
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   

RevsToCollect
   

   
12
   
   
 
   
   
RevsToCollect is the number of servo revolutions worth of PES data to collect.
   
  

  

   
13
   
   
 
   
  

  

   

reserved
   

   
14..15
   
   
 
   
   
reserved
   
  




  Diagnostic Status Block:


  

   Name
   Byte
Index		
   Value
   Description

Dsb (Structure, Length=30010)

Dsb is a binary servo data Diagnostic Status Block (DSB).
    

  

  

   

Header (Structure, Length=8)

Header is the extrinsic Diagnostic Status Block (DSB) header.
    

  

  

   

DataTypeId
   

   
8
   
   
0x40
   
   
DataTypeId specifies the type of data being returned.  The allowed values are defined by

the "diag_data_type_id" enumeration.
   		
  

  

   
9
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   

RevisionId
   

   
10
   
   
0x01
   
   
RevisionId specifies the revision of the diagnostic data returned by the diagnostic

function.
   		
  

  

   
11
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   

Error
   

   
12
   
   
 
   
   
Error contains the Diagnostic Test Service error code.  See the link below for all the

supported error codes.

Diagnostic Error Codes
   		
  

  

   
13
   
   
 
   
  

  

   
14
   
   
 
   
  

  

   
15
   
   
 
   
  

  

   

NumberOfServoData
   

   
16
   
   
 
   
   
NumberOfServoData is the number of servo data elements that was collected

in ServoData (see below).
   		
  

  

   
17
   
   
 
   
  

  

   

ServoData
   

   
2i+18
   
   
 
   
   
ServoData is an array of servo data (16 bit).

Where:

   i = 0 to 14999
   		
  

  

   
2i+19

 Format Partition


  Description:
    This diagnostic mode function performs a format and defect mapping operation on the
    specified media partition.  A format can perform reads and writes of the entire disk
    pack, perform some manipulation of defect lists, and detect and deallocate or slip
    around defective sectors.

  Diagnostic Function Block (Revision 1):


  

   Name
   Byte
Index		
   Value
   Description
  

  

   

SdbpHeader (Structure, Length=8)

SdbpHeader is Seagate Diagnostic Bridge / Router Protocol (SDBP) packet header.
    

  

  

   

FromPort
   

   
0
   
   
0x07
   
   
FromPort is the SDBP Port on the host or drive where this packet came from.
   
  

  

   
1
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   

ToPort
   

   
2
   
   
0x07
   
   
ToPort is the SDBP Port on the host or drive where this packet is going.
   
  

  

   
3
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   

Length
   

   
4
   
   
0x20
   
   
Length is the length in bytes of the packet not including the SDBP packet header.
   
  

  

   
5
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   
6
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   
7
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   

Dfb (Structure, Length=32)

Dfb is the Diagnostic Function Block (DFB) for the Format Partition extrinsic diagnostic.
    

  

  

   

Header (Structure, Length=4)

Header is the extrinsic Diagnostic Function Block (DFB) header.
    

  

  

   

FunctionId
   

   
8
   
   
0x72
   
   
FunctionId is the ID of the diagnostic function to be executed.
   
  

  

   
9
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   

RevisionId
   

   
10
   
   
0x01
   
   
RevisionId is the revision of the parameters for the diagnostic function.
   
  

  

   
11
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   

PartitionId
   

   
12
   
   
 
   
   
PartitionId specifies which media partition is to be formatted.
   
  

  

   

reserved
   

   
13..15
   
   
 
   
   
reserved
   
  

  

   

FormatOptions (Structure, Length=4)

FormatOptions specifies options to be used during the format operation.
    

  

  

   

Bitfield:

CorruptUserPartitionPrimaryDefects

DisableUserPartitionFormat

DisableUserPartitionCertify

EnableEventBasedFormatLogging

SkipZoneReformat

EnableFormatXfSpace

unused
   

   
16
   
   
 
   
   
Bit 0:

CorruptUserPartitionPrimaryDefects, if TRUE, the primary defective sectors will

be corrupted when formatting the User Partition.



Bit 1:

DisableUserPartitionFormat, if TRUE, the User Partition sectors will not be written

with a constant data pattern.



Bit 2:

DisableUserPartitionCertify, if TRUE, media certification and defect deallocation

will be disabled when formatting the User Partition.



Bit 3:

EnableEventBasedFormatLogging, if TRUE, will enable the reporting of events experienced

by the Read/Write firmware as interim status.



Bit 4:

SkipZoneReformat, if TRUE, zone reformat will be skipped during format.



Bit 5:

EnableFormatXfSpace, if TRUE, will only format SeaCOS Extended File (XF) space.



Bits 6-31:

unused
   		
  

  

   
17
   
   
 
   
  

  

   
18
   
   
 
   
  

  

   
19
   
   
 
   
  

  

   

ProcessDefectListOptions (Structure, Length=4)

ProcessDefectListOptions specifies which defect lists are to be used for the format

operation.
    

  

  

   

Bitfield:

ProcessGrownDefectLists

ProcessPrimaryDefectLists

ProcessActiveErrorLog

unused
   

   
20
   
   
 
   
   
Bit 0:

ProcessGrownDefectLists, if TRUE, the Grown Defect Lists will be used when

creating the defect list to be used to format the User Partition.



Bit 1:

ProcessPrimaryDefectLists, if TRUE, the Primary Defect Lists will be used when

creating the defect list to be used to format the User Partition.



Bit 2:

ProcessActiveErrorLog, if TRUE, the R/W-related entries in the Active Error Log will

be written to the Format Client Defect List and the option to include the Format

Client Defect List in the Processed Defect List will be enabled.



Bits 3-31:

unused
   		
  

  

   
21
   
   
 
   
  

  

   
22
   
   
 
   
  

  

   
23
   
   
 
   
  

  

   

RetryConfigOptions (Structure, Length=3)

RetryConfigOptions specifies which retry parameters are to be modified for the

format operation.
    

  

  

   

SelectMaxWriteRetryCount
   

   
24
   
   
 
   
   
SelectMaxWriteRetryCount, if TRUE, indicates that a new maximum write retry count has

been specified for a diagnostic format operation.
   		
  

  

   

SelectMaxReadRetryCount
   

   
25
   
   
 
   
   
SelectMaxReadRetryCount, if TRUE, indicates that a new maximum read retry count has

been specified for a diagnostic format operation.
   		
  

  

   

SelectMaxEccTLevel
   

   
26
   
   
 
   
   
SelectMaxEccTLevel, if TRUE, indicates that a new maximum ECC T-Level has been

specified for a diagnostic format operation.
   		
  

  

   

reserved
   

   
27
   
   
 
   
   
reserved
   
  

  

   

RetryConfig (Structure, Length=6)

RetryConfig specifies the retry parameters to for the format operation.
    

  

  

   

MaxWriteRetryCount
   

   
28
   
   
 
   
   
MaxWriteRetryCount is the maximum Write Retry Count to be used.
   
  

  

   
29
   
   
 
   
  

  

   

MaxReadRetryCount
   

   
30
   
   
 
   
   
MaxReadRetryCount is the maximum Read Retry Count to be used.
   
  

  

   
31
   
   
 
   
  

  

   

MaxEccTLevel
   

   
32
   
   
 
   
   
MaxEccTLevel is the maximum ECC T-Level to be used.
   
  

  

   
33
   
   
 
   
  

  

   

CertifyRewriteRetryThresholdValid
   

   
34
   
   
 
   
   
CertifyRewriteRetryThresholdValid, if TRUE, the maximum number of rewrite retries

to be performed during the user partition certification pass is specified by

CertifyRewriteRetryThreshold.  If CertifyRewriteRetryThresholdValid is FALSE,

the maximum number of rewrite retries to be performed during the user partition

certification pass should be set equal to the default value.
   		
  

  

   

reserved
   

   
35
   
   
 
   
   
reserved
   
  

  

   

CertifyRewriteRetryThreshold
   

   
36
   
   
 
   
   
CertifyRewriteRetryThreshold specifies the maximum number of rewrite retries to be

performed during the user partition certification pass.
   		
  

  

   
37
   
   
 
   
  

  

   

reserved

are supported are given below.


0: RW_FORMAT_LOG_FORMAT_MEDIA_ZONE_START_EVENT indicates that the format

   event is a format media zone start event.

1: RW_FORMAT_LOG_FORMAT_XFR_EVENT indicates that the format event is a

   format transfer event.

2: RW_FORMAT_LOG_UNRECOVERED_ERROR_EVENT indicates that the format event

   is an unrecovered error event.

3: RW_FORMAT_LOG_CERTIFY_TRACK_REWRITE_EVENT indicates that the format

   event is a certify track rewrite event.

4: RW_FORMAT_LOG_CERTIFY_TRACK_REWRITE_COUNT_UPDATE_EVENT indicates that

   the format event is certify track rewrite count update event.

5: RW_FORMAT_LOG_DEALLOCATE_DEFECTIVE_BLOCK_EVENT indicates that the

   format event is a deallocate defective block event.

completed successfully without the use of error recovery, it will be equal to

RW_REQUEST_SATISFIED (0). If the operation completed successfully with the use of error

recovery, it will be equal to RW_REQUEST_SATISFIED_WITH_RECOVERY (1).  If the operation

completed with an error condition, it will be equal to RW_REQUEST_FAILED (2).

 Generic Servo Command


  Description:
    This diagnostic mode diagnostic function sends the generic servo command that is
    specified by the input parameters.  WARNING: USE WITH CAUTION!  This function can
    send servo commands that may significantly change the state of the drive and
    without R/W firmware's awareness.  This may cause asserts.

  Diagnostic Function Block:


  

   Name
   Byte
Index		
   Value
   Description
  

  

   

SdbpHeader (Structure, Length=8)

SdbpHeader is Seagate Diagnostic Bridge / Router Protocol (SDBP) packet header.
    

  

  

   

FromPort
   

   
0
   
   
0x07
   
   
FromPort is the SDBP Port on the host or drive where this packet came from.
   
  

  

   
1

VbarAdjustableZoneBoundariesEnabled, if TRUE, indicates that VBAR is enabled and the

zone boundaries are adjustable.

VolumeBasedSparingEnabled, if TRUE, indicates that volume sparing is enabled.

839
   
   
 
   
   
IoedcEnabled, if TRUE, indicates that IOEDC is enabled.
   
  

  

   

IoeccEnabled
   

   
840
   
   
 
   
   
IoeccEnabled, if TRUE, indicates that IOECC is enabled.
   
  

  

   

DerpReadRetriesEnabled
   

   
841
   
   
 
   
   
DerpReadRetriesEnabled, if TRUE, indicates that DERP read retries is enabled.
   
  

  

   

Udr2Info
   

   
842
   
   
 
   
   
Udr2Info contains information about if UDR 2 recovery is enabled or compiled in.


0x00: UDR2_RECOVERY_UNSUPPORTED indicates that UDR2 Recovery is not supported

by the firmware.

0x01: UDR2_RECOVERY_DISABLED indicates that UDR2 recovery has been disabled

because the number PowerOn Life hours has exceeded the LTTCPowerOnHours or

because a write long has occurred.

0x02: UDR2_RECOVERY_ENABLED indicates that UDR2 recovery is allowed if all

other retries have been exhausted.

   		
  

  

   

reserved
   

   
843
   
   
 
   
   
reserved

Index

FromPort
   

   
0
   
   
0x07

0x00

SectorSplitInfo (Structure, Length=8)

SectorSplitInfo contains information about a sector that is split by a servo burst.
    

  

  

   

PreceedingServoBurst
   

   
68i+94
   
   
 
   
   
PreceedingServoBurst is the number of the servo burst that preceeds it.
   
  

  

   
68i+95
   
   
 
   
  

  

   

SplitServoBurst
   

   
68i+96
   
   
 
   
   
SplitServoBurst is the number of the the servo burst that splits the sector.  If the

sector is not split, this will be equal to INVALID_SERVO_WEDGE.
   		
  

  

   
68i+97
   
   
 
   
  

  

   

StartingFragmentBytes
   

   
68i+98
   
   
 
   
   
StartingFragmentBytes is the number of bytes in the first part of a split sector or

the total number of data bytes in the sector if it is unsplit.
   		
  

  

   
68i+99
   
   
 
   
  

  

   

EndingFragmentBytes
   

   
68i+100
   
   
 
   
   
EndingFragmentBytes is the number of bytes in the second half of a split sector.  If

the secor is unsplit, this will be equal to 0.
   		
  

  

   
68i+101
   
   
 
   
  

  

   

reserved
   

   
68i+102..103
   
   
 
   
   
reserved

ReallocationStatus
   

   
68i+104

0x00: LBA_NOT_REALLOCATED_WITH_PBA_MARKED_DEFECTIVE

0x01: LBA_NOT_REALLOCATED

0x02: LBA_REALLOCATED

0x03: LBA_REALLOCATION_PENDING

0x04: LBA_REALLOCATED_REALLOCATION_PENDING

   		
  

  

   

reserved
   

   
68i+105..107
   
   
 
   
   
reserved

68i+109
   
   
 
   
  

  

   
68i+110
   
   
 
   
  

  

   
68i+111

68i+112
   
   
 
   
   
SymbolsFromIndexValid, if TRUE, indicates that SymbolsFromIndex is valid.
   
  

  

   

reserved
   

   
68i+113..115
   
   
 
   
   
reserved

 Initialize Defect Lists


  Description:
    This diagnostic mode function will initialize one or more defect lists to contain no
    defects.  Optionally it will write the cleared list(s) to disk to make the change
    permanent.

    Note: This diagnostic function supports two revisions of its Diagnostic Function Block
    at run-time.

  Diagnostic Function Block (Revision 1):


  

   Name
   Byte
Index		
   Value
   Description

Options (Structure, Length=4)

Options specifies which defect lists are to be initialized.
    

  

  

   

Bitfield:

InitUserSlipList

Reserved1

InitUserAltList

Reserved2

SaveToDisk
   

   
12
   
   
 
   
   
Bit 0:

InitUserSlipList when set indicates that the user slip list should be initialized.



Bit 1:

Reserved1 for possible additional option-specifier bits.  It should be set to zero

for future compatibility.



Bit 2:

InitUserAltList when set indicates that the user alt list should be initialized.



Bits 3-30:

Reserved2 is set aside for possible additional option-specifier bits.  They should

be set to zero for future compatibility.



Bit 31:

SaveToDisk, when set, indicates that the selected list should be saved to disk

after initialization.

Bitfield:

InitUserSlipList

Reserved1

InitUserAltList

Reserved
   

   
12
   
   
 
   
   
Bit 0:

InitUserSlipList when set indicates that the user slip list should be operated on.



Bit 1:

Reserved1 for possible additional option-specifier bits.  It should be set to zero

for future compatibility.



Bit 2:

InitUserAltList when set indicates that the user alt list should be operated on.



Bits 3-31:

be set to zero for future compatibility.

ListMode
   

   
16
   
   
 
   
   
ListMode specifies how list is to initialized (zeroed, read from disk, etc)


0x00: INITIALIZE_TO_ZERO_AND_SAVE indicates that the list should be zeroed and saved to

nonvolatile storage.

0x01: INITIALIZE_TO_ZERO_DO_NOT_SAVE indicates that the list should be zeroed but not saved.

0x02: READ_FROM_NONVOLATILE_MEMORY indicates that the list should be read from nonvolatile

memory, overwriting what is in volatile memory.

StartingTimeStamp (Structure, Length=8)

StartingTimeStamp is the time stamp at the start of the last read/write operation.
    

  

  

   

TimestampBits00Thru15
   

   
24
   
   
 
   
   
TimestampBits00Thru15 holds the least significant 16 bits of the 48-bit

time stamp.

26
   
   
 
   
   
TimestampBits16Thru31 holds the middle 16 bits of the 48-bit time stamp.
   
  

  

   
27

28
   
   
 
   
   
TimestampBits32Thru47 holds the most significant 16 bits of the 48-bit

time stamp.
   		
  

  

   
29

30
   
   
 
   
   
PowerCycleCount is the current count of the number of power cycles.
   
  

  

   
31
   
   
 
   
  

  

   

ElapsedTimeInUsec
   

   
32
   
   
 
   
   
ElapsedTimeInUsec is the number of microseconds it took to complete the last read/write

operation.
   		
  

  

   
33
   
   
 
   
  

  

   
34
   
   
 
   
  

  

   
35
   
   
 
   
  

  

   

SystemAreaAccess
   

   
36
   
   
 
   
   
SystemAreaAccess will be equal to TRUE, if the last read/write operation accessed the

System Area.
   		
  

  

   

WedgeMode
   

   
37
   
   
 
   
   
WedgeMode be equal to TRUE, if the last read/write operation was a wedge read or write.
   
  

  

   

SeekType
   

   
38
   
   
 
   
   
SeekType contains the type of the last seek performed.  The following are valid seek

types:


0x00: DIAG_READ_SEEK - Indicates a seek to the read track follow position.

0x01: DIAG_WRITE_SEEK - Indicates a seek to the write track follow position.

0x02: DIAG_WRITE_HEADER_SEEK - Indicates a seek to the write header track follow position.

   		
  

  

   

SeekSpeedEnabled
   

   
39
   
   
 
   
   
SeekSpeedEnabled, if TRUE, indicates that the JIT seek speed specified by SeekSpeed

has been enabled for diagnostic seek, read and write operations.
   		
  

  

   

SeekSpeed
   

   
40
   
   
 
   
   
SeekSpeed specifies the JIT seek speed to be used for diagnostic seek, read and write

operations, if SeekSpeedEnabled is equal to TRUE.  The following are valid seek speeds:


0x00: RW_SEEK_SPEED_0 - Indicates normal seeks should be executed.

0x01: RW_SEEK_SPEED_1 - If supported, indicates JIT1 seeks should be executed.

0x02: RW_SEEK_SPEED_2 - If supported, indicates JIT2 seeks should be executed.

0x03: RW_SEEK_SPEED_3 - If supported, indicates JIT3 seeks should be executed.

   		
  

  

   

reserved
   

   
41
   
   
 
   
   
reserved

42
   
   
 
   
   
SeekTimeInServoBursts contains the seek time in servo bursts.
   
  

  

   
43
   
   
 
   
  

  

   

PersistentTrackFollowOffsetPercentValid
   

   
44
   
   
 
   
   
PersistentTrackFollowOffsetPercentValid, if TRUE, indicates that the Total Track

Follow Offset should be calculated based on the Persistent Track Follow Offset

percentage.  If FALSE, the Total Track Follow Offset should be calculated based

on the Persistent Track Follow Offset count.
   		
  

  

   

reserved
   

   
45
   
   
 
   
   
reserved
   
  

  

   

PersistentTrackFollowOffsetPercent
   

   
46
   
   
 
   
   
PersistentTrackFollowOffsetPercent is the persistent track follow offset in units of

0.1% of the data track width.  It will be applied on the next seek and all subsequent

seeks until reset.  This a signed, 2's complement value.
   		
  

  

   
47
   
   
 
   
  

  

   

PersistentTrackFollowOffsetCount
   

   
48
   
   
 
   
   
PersistentTrackFollowOffsetCount is the persistent track follow offset in units

of 1/256th of the servo track width.  It will be applied on the next seek and all

subsequent seeks until reset.  This is a signed, 2's complement value.
   		
  

  

   
49
   
   
 
   
  

  

   

TemporaryTrackFollowOffsetPercentValid
   

   
50
   
   
 
   
   
TemporaryTrackFollowOffsetPercentValid, if TRUE, indicates that the Total Track

Follow Offset should be calculated based on the Temporary Track Follow Offset

percentage.  If FALSE, the Total Track Follow Offset should be calculated based

on the Temporary Track Follow Offset count.
   		
  

  

   

reserved
   

   
51
   
   
 
   
   
reserved
   
  

  

   

TemporaryTrackFollowOffsetPercent
   

   
52
   
   
 
   
   
TemporaryTrackFollowOffsetPercent is the temporary track follow offset in units of

0.1% of the data track width.  It will be applied on the next seek, but will be reset

to zero for all subsequent seeks.  This is a signed, 2's complement value.
   		
  

  

   
53
   
   
 
   
  

  

   

TemporaryTrackFollowOffsetCount
   

   
54
   
   
 
   
   
TemporaryTrackFollowOffsetCount is the temporary track follow offset in units of

1/256th of the servo track width.  It will be applied on the next seek, but will be

reset to zero for all subsequent seeks.  This is a signed, 2's complement value.
   		
  

  

   
55
   
   
 
   
  

  

   

TotalTrackFollowOffsetPercent
   

   
56
   
   
 
   
   
TotalTrackFollowOffsetPercent is the total track follow offset applied on the last

seek.  It  is equal to the sum of the persistent and temporary offset.  It is in

units of 0.1% of the data track width.  This is a signed, 2's complement value.
   		
  

  

   
57
   
   
 
   
  

  

   

TotalTrackFollowOffsetCount
   

   
58
   
   
 
   
   
TotalTrackFollowOffsetCount is the total track follow offset in units of 1/256th of the

 Measure Disc Eccentricity


  Description:
    This diagnostic mode function will measure the disc eccentricity. The measurement will be
    done for all heads at a cylinder location called the zero-skew cylinder. The zero-skew
    cylinder is calculated to be two-thirds of the stroke from the disc OD.

 Modify Track Defect List


  Description:
    This diagnostic mode function will modify the track defect list for the target address
    or for all sectors on the target track based in the input.  The track can be modified to
    show that the specified sector is alternated, is in the pending defect list, is defect-
    free, is in the user area slip list, is in the reserved area slip list, or is removed
    from the alternate list.

  Diagnostic Function Block:


  

   Name
   Byte
Index		
   Value
   Description

ModificationType
   

   
16
   
   
 
   
   
ModificationType specifies the type of defect list modification to be

performed.


0x0A: ADD_TO_ALT_LIST - The given CHS should be added to the alt list.

0x0B: ADD_TO_PENDING_LIST - The given CHS should be added to the pending list.

0xA1: ADD_LBA_TO_ALT_LIST - The given LBA should be added to the alt list.

0xB1: ADD_LBA_TO_PENDING_LIST - The given CHS should be added to the pending list.

0xC1: REMOVE_LBA_FROM_ALL - The given LBA should be removed from all defect lists.

0xF1: REMOVE_LBA_FROM_ALT_LIST - The given LBA should be removed from the alt list.

Header is the extrinsic Diagnostic Function Block (DFB) header.

8
   
   
0x13
   
   
FunctionId is the ID of the diagnostic function to be executed.

0x01
   
   
RevisionId is the revision of the parameters for the diagnostic function.
   
  

  

   
11
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   

MaxHeadData (Structure, Length=2)

MaxHeadData contains the new Max Head to be written to servo's SAP.
    

  

  

   

SapOperation
   

   
12
   
   
 
   
   
SapOperation is a bit-significant value that indicates whether the Max Head should be

read from or written to the SAP.
   		
  

  

   

MaxHead
   

   
13
   
   
 
   
   
MaxHead is the maximum number of heads supported by the servo.
   
  

  

   

MrBiasData (Structure, Length=28)

MrBiasData contains the new MR bias values to write to servo's SAP.  NOTE: The data

values include the preamp register address that represents the MR bias.
    

  

  

   

SapOperation
   

   
14
   
   
 
   
   
SapOperation is a bit-significant value that indicates whether one, none, or all of the

SAP data values are valid and whether or not the values should be read from or written to

the SAP.


Bit 0: If set, then a write operation will be performed and the written values will be

       mirrored in the Diagnostic Status Block.  (Setting this bit overrides the state of

       bit 1.)

Bit 1: If set, then a read operation will be performed.  (This bit is meaningful only if

       bit 0 is not set.)

Bit 2: If set, a read or write operation will be performed for all values.  If not set, then

       the operation will be performed on the specified value only.  (This bit is only

       meaningful if either bit 0 or bit 1 is also set.)

   		
  

  

   

Head
   

   
15
   
   
 
   
   
Head is the index into the table of data values.  When used in either the DFB or DSB and

if it makes sense according to the value in SapOperation, it indicates which head the

data value is valid for.
   		
  

  

   

MaxHead
   

   
16
   
   
 
   
   
MaxHead is the maximum number of heads supported by the servo.  NOTE: This value is

only valid when used in the DSB.  The extrinsic function ignores it in the DFB.
   		
  

  

   

reserved
   

   
17
   
   
 
   
   
reserved
   
  

  

   

Data
   

   
2i+18
   
   
 
   
   
Data is an array of 16-bit values indexed by head that represents MR bias information.

Where:

   i = 0 to 11
   		
  

  

   
2i+19
   
   
 
   
  

  

   

MaxMrBiasData (Structure, Length=28)

MaxMrBiasData contains the new maximum safe MR bias values to be written to servo's SAP.
    

  

  

   

SapOperation
   

   
42
   
   
 
   
   
SapOperation is a bit-significant value that indicates whether one, none, or all of the

SAP data values are valid and whether or not the values should be read from or written to

the SAP.


Bit 0: If set, then a write operation will be performed and the written values will be

       mirrored in the Diagnostic Status Block.  (Setting this bit overrides the state of

       bit 1.)

Bit 1: If set, then a read operation will be performed.  (This bit is meaningful only if

       bit 0 is not set.)

Bit 2: If set, a read or write operation will be performed for all values.  If not set, then

       the operation will be performed on the specified value only.  (This bit is only

       meaningful if either bit 0 or bit 1 is also set.)

   		
  

  

   

Head
   

   
43
   
   
 
   
   
Head is the index into the table of data values.  When used in either the DFB or DSB and

if it makes sense according to the value in SapOperation, it indicates which head the

data value is valid for.
   		
  

  

   

MaxHead
   

   
44

data value is valid for.

16

only valid when used in the DSB.  The extrinsic function ignores it in the DFB.
   		
  

  

   

reserved
   

   
17
   
   
 
   
   
reserved

2i+18

Where:

   i = 0 to 11

MaxMrBiasData (Structure, Length=28)

MaxMrBiasData contains the new maximum safe MR bias values to be written to servo's SAP.
    

  

  

   

SapOperation
   

   
42
   
   
 
   
   
SapOperation is a bit-significant value that indicates whether one, none, or all of the

SAP data values are valid and whether or not the values should be read from or written to

the SAP.


Bit 0: If set, then a write operation will be performed and the written values will be

       mirrored in the Diagnostic Status Block.  (Setting this bit overrides the state of

       bit 1.)

Bit 1: If set, then a read operation will be performed.  (This bit is meaningful only if

       bit 0 is not set.)

Bit 2: If set, a read or write operation will be performed for all values.  If not set, then

       the operation will be performed on the specified value only.  (This bit is only

       meaningful if either bit 0 or bit 1 is also set.)

   		
  

  

   

Head
   

   
43
   
   
 
   
   
Head is the index into the table of data values.  When used in either the DFB or DSB and

if it makes sense according to the value in SapOperation, it indicates which head the

data value is valid for.

 Read Servo RAM At Index


  Description:
    This diagnostic mode function reads the contents of Servo RAM located at the address
    obtained from the Servo Symbol Table at the specified index.

    WARNING: this function does NOT check whether the contents of the Servo Symbol Table
    located at the specified index is a valid memory location since servo does not make
    this information available to the firmware.

  Diagnostic Function Block:


  

   Name
   Byte
Index		
   Value
   Description
  

  

   

SdbpHeader (Structure, Length=8)

SdbpHeader is Seagate Diagnostic Bridge / Router Protocol (SDBP) packet header.
    

  

  

   

FromPort
   

   
0
   
   
0x07
   
   
FromPort is the SDBP Port on the host or drive where this packet came from.
   
  

  

   
1
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   

ToPort
   

   
2
   
   
0x07
   
   
ToPort is the SDBP Port on the host or drive where this packet is going.
   
  

  

   
3
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   

Length
   

   
4
   
   
0x0C
   
   
Length is the length in bytes of the packet not including the SDBP packet header.

0x00

0x00

 Reset Drive


  Description:
    This Online Mode diagnostic function will either reset the drive or jump to the Boot
    Strap Loader.  NOTE: Once invoked, this function will not return and the host-side test
    environment will have to accommodate this.

  Diagnostic Function Block:


  

   Name
   Byte
Index		
   Value

 Set Selected DERP Retry State


  Description:
    This diagnostic mode function will set the Selected DERP Retry State that will be used
    for subsequent diagnostic operations.

  Diagnostic Function Block:


  

   Name
   Byte
Index		
   Value
   Description
  

  

   

SdbpHeader (Structure, Length=8)

SdbpHeader is Seagate Diagnostic Bridge / Router Protocol (SDBP) packet header.
    

  

  

   

FromPort
   

   
0
   
   
0x07
   
   
FromPort is the SDBP Port on the host or drive where this packet came from.
   
  

  

   
1
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   

ToPort
   

   
2
   
   
0x07
   
   
ToPort is the SDBP Port on the host or drive where this packet is going.
   
  

  

   
3
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   

Length
   

   
4
   
   
0x0A
   
   
Length is the length in bytes of the packet not including the SDBP packet header.
   
  

  

   
5
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   
6
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   
7
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   

Dfb (Structure, Length=10)

Dfb is the Diagnostic Function Block (DFB) for the Set DERP Retry State extrinsic

diagnostic.
    

  

  

   

Header (Structure, Length=4)

Header is the extrinsic Diagnostic Function Block (DFB) header.
    

  

  

   

FunctionId
   

   
8
   
   
0x16
   
   
FunctionId is the ID of the diagnostic function to be executed.
   
  

  

   
9
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   

RevisionId
   

   
10
   
   
0x01
   
   
RevisionId is the revision of the parameters for the diagnostic function.
   
  

  

   
11
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   

EnableDerpRetryState
   

   
12
   
   
 
   
   
EnableDerpRetryState, if TRUE, will enable the Selected DERP Retry State and the new

values are required in DerpRetryState.  If FALSE, it will disable the Selected DERP Retry

State.
   		
  

  

   

DerpRetryState (Structure, Length=5)

DerpRetryState contains the new DERP Retry State values.  (These parameters are ignored

if EnableDerpRetryState is set to FALSE.
    

  

  

   

Type
   

   
13
   
   
 
   
   
Type specifies the type of error that the DERP Error Recovery system will assume

for disc access operations.  (Only valid if the drive supports DERP.)


0 = UNDETERMINED

1 = DATA_ERROR

2 = SYNC

3 = TA

4 = DATAORTA

5 = SYNCTA

6 = SYNCORDATA

   		
  

  

   

PathState
   

   
14
   
   
 
   
   
DerpPathState specifies the path count from the current retry sequence that the DERP Error

Recovery system will assume for disc access operations.  The meaning of the Path State

is dependent on the Error Type (parameter 0).  (Only valid if the drive supports DERP.)
   		
  

  

   

RetryStateCnt
   

   
15
   
   
 
   
   
DerpRetryStateCnt specifies the retry path count from the current retry sequence that the

DERP Error Recovery system will assume for disc access operations.  (Only valid if the

drive supports DERP.)
   		
  

  

   

LoopCntr1
   

   
16
   
   
 
   
   
DerpLoopCntr1 specifies the first loop counter that the DERP Error Recovery system will

assume for disc access operations.  (Only valid if the drive supports DERP.)
   		
  

  

   

LoopCntr2
   

   
17
   
   
 
   
   
DerpLoopCntr2 specifies the second loop counter that the DERP Error Recovery system will

assume for disc access operations.  (Only valid if the drive supports DERP.)
   		
  

  

   

reserved
   

   
18..19
   
   
 
   
   
reserved

 Set Target Address


  Description:
    This diagnostic mode function sets the Test Space's target address based on the values
    specified in the Diagnostic Function Block.

  Diagnostic Function Block:


  

   Name
   Byte
Index		
   Value
   Description
  

  

   

SdbpHeader (Structure, Length=8)

SdbpHeader is Seagate Diagnostic Bridge / Router Protocol (SDBP) packet header.
    

  

  

   

FromPort
   

   
0
   
   
0x07
   
   
FromPort is the SDBP Port on the host or drive where this packet came from.
   
  

  

   
1
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   

ToPort
   

   
2
   
   
0x07
   
   
ToPort is the SDBP Port on the host or drive where this packet is going.
   
  

  

   
3
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   

Length
   

   
4
   
   
0x18
   
   
Length is the length in bytes of the packet not including the SDBP packet header.
   
  

  

   
5
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   
6
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   
7
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   

Dfb (Structure, Length=24)

Dfb is the Diagnostic Function Block (DFB) for the Set Target Address extrinsic

diagnostic.
    

  

  

   

Header (Structure, Length=4)

Header is the extrinsic Diagnostic Function Block (DFB) header.
    

  

  

   

FunctionId
   

   
8
   
   
0x25
   
   
FunctionId is the ID of the diagnostic function to be executed.
   
  

  

   
9
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   

RevisionId
   

   
10
   
   
0x01
   
   
RevisionId is the revision of the parameters for the diagnostic function.
   
  

  

   
11
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   

TargetAddrMode
   

   
12
   
   
 
   
   
TargetAddrMode specifies the Address Mode to be selected:



0x00: USER_LBA_ADDR_MODE specifies that the User Area will be accessed in LBA mode.

0x01: USER_LLL_CHS_ADDR_MODE specifies that the User Area will be accessed in Logical

Cylinder, Logical Head and Logical Sector mode.

0x02: USER_LLP_CHW_ADDR_MODE specifies that the User Area will be accessed in Logical

Cylinder, Logical Head and Physical Wedge mode.

0x03: SYSTEM_LBA_ADDR_MODE specifies that the System Area will be accessed in LBA mode.

0x04: SYSTEM_LLL_CHS_ADDR_MODE specifies that the System Area will be accessed in Logical

Cylinder, Logical Head and Logical Sector mode.

0x05: SYSTEM_LLP_CHW_ADDR_MODE specifies that the System Area will be accessed in Logical

Cylinder, Logical Head and Physical Wedge mode.

0x06: PLP_CHS_ADDR_MODE specifies that the full drive will be accessed in Physical Cylinder,

Logical Head and Physical Sector mode.

0x07: PLP_CHW_ADDR_MODE specifies that the full drive will be accessed in Physical Cylinder,

Logical Head and Physical Wedge mode.

   		
  

  

   

UpdateTargetAddrOption
   

   
13
   
   
 
   
   
UpdateTargetAddrOption specifies the option selected for updating the Target Address:



0x00: DO_NOT_UPDATE_TARGET_ADDR - Indicates that the Target Address is not to be updated.

0x01: UPDATE_TARGET_ADDR - Indicates that the Target Address is to be updated based on

the Test Space that is selected.

0x02: UPDATE_TARGET_HD - Indicates that the Target Head Address is to be updated based

on the Test Space that is selected.  This option is only valid for the following Address

Modes: USER_LLL_CHS_ADDR_MODE, USER_LLP_CHW_ADDR_MODE, SYSTEM_LLL_CHS_ADDR_MODE,

SYSTEM_LLP_CHW_ADDR_MODE, PLP_CHS_ADDR_MODE, PLP_CHW_ADDR_MODE.
   		
  

  

   

SetTargetAddrOption
   

   
14
   
   
 
   
   
SetTargetAddrOption specifies the option selected for setting the Target Address:



0x00: DO_NOT_SET_TARGET_ADDR indicates that the Target Address is not to be modified.

0x01: SET_TARGET_LBA indicates that a new Target LBA is being specified.

0x02: SET_TARGET_CHS_OR_CHW indicates that a new Target Cylinder, Head and Sector (or

Wedge) address are being specified.

0x03: SET_TARGET_CYL indicates that a new Target Cylinder address is being specified.

0x04: SET_TARGET_HD indicates that a new Target Head address is being specified.

0x05: SET_TARGET_SECTOR_OR_WEDGE indicates that a new Target Sector or Wedge address is

being specified.

0x06: SET_TARGET_ADDR_TO_CURRENT_RW_ADDR indicates that the Target Address should be

set to the current R/W Address.
   		
  

  

   

reserved
   

   
15
   
   
 
   
   
reserved
   
  

  

   

TargetAddr (Union, Length=8)

TargetAddr specifies the value, if any, to which the Target Address is to be set.
    

  

  

   

Lba
   

   
16
   
   
 
   
   
Lba is used to specify a new Target LBA.
   
  

  

   
17
   
   
 
   
  

  

   
18
   
   
 
   
  

  

   
19
   
   
 
   
  

  

   

reserved
   

   
20..23
   
   
 
   
   
reserved
   
  

  

   

ChsOrChw (Structure, Length=8)

ChsOrChw is used to specify a new Target Cylinder, Head and Sector (or Wedge) address.
    

  

  

   

Cylinder
   

   
16
   
   
 
   
   
Cylinder is the cylinder address of the sector or wedge.
   
  

  

   
17
   
   
 
   
  

  

   
18
   
   
 
   
  

  

   
19
   
   
 
   
  

  

   

Head

ParmType
   

   
12
   
   
 
   
   
ParmType specifies the Test Space Parameter to be modified.

0x00: NO_TEST_SPACE_PARM - indicates that no Test Space parameter is to be modified.

0x01: SET_DEFAULT_TEST_SPACE - indicates that the Test Space parameters should be set

to = 0x01 their default values.

0x02: SET_TARGET_ADDR_MODE - indicates that a new Address Mode (User LBA, User LLL

CHS, User LLP CHW, System LBA, System LLL CHS, System LLP CHW, PLP CHS or PLP CHW) is

being specified.

0x03: SET_TEST_SPACE_OPTIONS - indicates that new Test Space Options are being

specified.

0x04: SET_TEST_SPACE_MIN_USER_LLL_CHS_CYL - indicates that a new Test Space Minimum

Logical Cylinder Address is being specified for User LLL CHS address mode.

0x05: SET_TEST_SPACE_MIN_SYSTEM_LLL_CHS_CYL - indicates that a new Test Space Minimum

Logical Cylinder Address is being specified for System LLL CHS address mode.

0x06: SET_TEST_SPACE_MIN_PLP_CHS_CYL - indicates that a new Test Space Minimum Physical

Cylinder Address is being specified for PLP CHS address mode.

0x07: SET_TEST_SPACE_MAX_USER_LLL_CHS_CYL - indicates that a new Test Space Maximum

Logical Cylinder Address is being specified for User LLL CHS address mode.

0x08: SET_TEST_SPACE_MAX_SYSTEM_LLL_CHS_CYL - indicates that a new Test Space Maximum

Logical Cylinder Address is being specified for System LLL CHS address mode.

0x09: SET_TEST_SPACE_MAX_PLP_CHS_CYL - indicates that a new Test Space Maximum Physical

Cylinder Address is being specified for PLP CHS address mode.

0x0A: SET_TEST_SPACE_MIN_USER_LLL_CHS_HD - indicates that a new Test Space Minimum

Logical Head Address is being specified for User LLL CHS address mode.

0x0B: SET_TEST_SPACE_MIN_SYSTEM_LLL_CHS_HD - indicates that a new Test Space Minimum

Logical Head Address is being specified for System LLL CHS address mode.

0x0C: SET_TEST_SPACE_MIN_PLP_CHS_HD - indicates that a new Test Space Minimum Logical

Head Address is being specified for PLP CHS address mode.

0x0D: SET_TEST_SPACE_MAX_USER_LLL_CHS_HD - indicates that a new Test Space Maximum

Logical Head Address is being specified for User LLL CHS address mode.

0x0E: SET_TEST_SPACE_MAX_SYSTEM_LLL_CHS_HD - indicates that a new Test Space Maximum

Logical Head Address is being specified for System LLL CHS address mode.

0x0F: SET_TEST_SPACE_MAX_PLP_CHS_HD - indicates that a new Test Space Maximum Logical

Head Address is being specified for PLP CHS address mode.

0x10: SET_TEST_SPACE_MIN_USER_LBA - indicates that a new Test Space Minimum LBA is

being specified for User LBA address mode.

0x11: SET_TEST_SPACE_MIN_SYSTEM_LBA - indicates that a new Test Space Minimum LBA is

being specified for System LBA address mode.

0x12: SET_TEST_SPACE_MAX_USER_LBA - indicates that a new Test Space Maximum LBA is

being specified for User LBA address mode.

0x13: SET_TEST_SPACE_MAX_SYSTEM_LBA - indicates that a new Test Space Maximum LBA is

being specified for System LBA address mode.

0x14: SET_TARGET_BUFFER_SECTOR_OFFSET - indicates that a new Buffer Sector Offset is

being specified.

ParmValue (Union, Length=8)

ParmValue specifies the new value for the Test Space Parameter specified by ParmType.
    

  

  

   

TargetAddrMode
   

   
16
   
   
 
   
   
TargetAddrMode specifies a new Target Address Mode.

0x00: USER_LBA_ADDR_MODE specifies that the User Area will be accessed in LBA mode.

0x01: USER_LLL_CHS_ADDR_MODE specifies that the User Area will be accessed in Logical

Cylinder, Logical Head and Logical Sector mode.

0x02: USER_LLP_CHW_ADDR_MODE specifies that the User Area will be accessed in Logical

Cylinder, Logical Head and Physical Wedge mode.

0x03: SYSTEM_LBA_ADDR_MODE specifies that the System Area will be accessed in LBA mode.

0x04: SYSTEM_LLL_CHS_ADDR_MODE specifies that the System Area will be accessed in Logical

Cylinder, Logical Head and Logical Sector mode.

0x05: SYSTEM_LLP_CHW_ADDR_MODE specifies that the System Area will be accessed in Logical

Cylinder, Logical Head and Physical Wedge mode.

0x06: PLP_CHS_ADDR_MODE specifies that the full drive will be accessed in Physical Cylinder,

Logical Head and Physical Sector mode.

0x07: PLP_CHW_ADDR_MODE specifies that the full drive will be accessed in Physical Cylinder,

Logical Head and Physical Wedge mode.

   		
  

  

   

reserved
   

   
17..23
   
   
 
   
   
reserved
   
  

  

   

Options (Structure, Length=4)

Options specifies new Test Space Options.
    

  

  

   

Bitfield:

AllHds

AllCyls

RandomCylAndHd

spare0

EvenCyls

OddCyls

SequentialOut

RandomData

RandomStartingSector

RandomTransferLength

spare1

Sequential80Random20

spare2
   

   
16
   
   
 
   
   
Bit 0:

AllHds, if TRUE, all heads (Minimum Head to Maximum Head) will be accessed.  If

FALSE, only the current head will be accessed.



Bit 1:

AllCyls, if TRUE, all cylinders (Minimum Cylinder to Maximum Cylinder) will be

accessed.  If FALSE, only the current cylinder will be accessed.



Bit 2:

RandomCylAndHd, if TRUE, the cylinder and head address will be updated randomly.

If FALSE, the cylinder and head address will be updated sequentially.



Bit 3:

spare0 is an unused bit.



Bit 4:

EvenCyls, if TRUE, only even numbered cylinders will be accessed.



Bit 5:

OddCyls, if TRUE, only odd numbered cylinders will be accessed.



Bit 6:

SequentialOut, if TRUE, the cylinder and head address will be updated sequentially

from the Inner Diameter to the Outer Diameter.  If FALSE, the cylinder and head

address will be updated sequentially from the Outer Diameter to the Inner Diameter.



Bit 7:

RandomData, if TRUE, random data will be used for disk write operations.  If FALSE,

the existing buffer data will be used for write operations.



Bit 8:

RandomStartingSector, if TRUE, a random starting sector will be used for read/write

operations.  If FALSE, read/write operations will start at sector 0.



Bit 9:

RandomTransferLength, if TRUE, a random transfer length will be used for read/write

operations.



Bit 10:

spare1 is an unused bit.



Bit 11:

Sequential80Random20, if TRUE, the cylinder and head address will be updated

sequentially 80% of the time and randomly 20% of the time.



Bits 12-31:

spare2 is a collection of unused bits.
   		
  

  

   
17
   
   
 
   
  

  

   
18
   
   
 
   
  

  

   
19
   
   
 
   
  

  

   

reserved

 Spin Up Drive


  Description:
    This Diagnostic Mode diagnostic function will spin the drive up.  It gives options to
    cause the drive to hold certain states during the spin up, including unlatching or
    loading off a ramp, acquiring AMs (aka Demod Sync), and track following.

  Diagnostic Function Block:


  

   Name
   Byte
Index		
   Value
   Description
  

  

   

SdbpHeader (Structure, Length=8)

SdbpHeader is Seagate Diagnostic Bridge / Router Protocol (SDBP) packet header.
    

  

  

   

FromPort
   

   
0
   
   
0x07
   
   
FromPort is the SDBP Port on the host or drive where this packet came from.
   
  

  

   
1
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   

ToPort
   

   
2
   
   
0x07
   
   
ToPort is the SDBP Port on the host or drive where this packet is going.
   
  

  

   
3
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   

Length
   

   
4
   
   
0x10
   
   
Length is the length in bytes of the packet not including the SDBP packet header.
   
  

  

   
5
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   
6
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   
7
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   

Dfb (Structure, Length=16)

Dfb is the Diagnostic Function Block (DFB) for the Spin Up Drive diagnostic.
    

  

  

   

Header (Structure, Length=4)

Header is the Diagnostic Function Block (DFB) header.
    

  

  

   

FunctionId
   

   
8
   
   
0x1C
   
   
FunctionId is the ID of the diagnostic function to be executed.
   
  

  

   
9
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   

RevisionId
   

   
10
   
   
0x01
   
   
RevisionId is the revision of the parameters for the diagnostic function.
   
  

  

   
11
   
   
0x00
   
  

  

   

SpinUpHoldState
   

   
12
   
   
 
   
   
SpinUpHoldState specifies the state in which the spin up operation will be held.

0x00: SPIN_UP_NO_HOLD - Drive should spin up normally.

0x01: ADVANCE_HOLD_STATE - Drive should advance to the next hold state.

0x02: RELEASE_HOLD - Drive should spin up normally from current state.

0x03: HOLD_BEFORE_UNLATCH - Drive should hold before unlatching or loading.

0x04: HOLD_BEFORE_DEMOD_SYNC - Drive should hold before acquiring AMs.

0x05: HOLD_BEFORE_TRACK_FOLLOW - Drive should hold before tracking.
   		
  

  

   

PhysicalCylValid
   

   
13
   
   
 
   
   
PhysicalCylValid, if TRUE, and SpinUpHoldState is not equal to SPIN_UP_NO_HOLD,

indicates that the PhysicalCyl is valid and specifies the address of the physical

cylinder on which the servo will attempt to track follow after spinning up.  If

PhysicalCylValid is FALSE or the SpinUpHoldState is equal to SPIN_UP_NO_HOLD,

the servo will attempt to track follow on the default physical cylinder after

spinning up.
   		
  

  

   

reserved
   

   
14..15
   
   
 
   
   
reserved
   
  

  

   

PhysicalCyl
   

   
16
   
   
 
   
   
PhysicalCyl is the address of the physical cylinder on which the servo will attempt

to track follow after spinning up.  It is only used when PhysicalCylValid is TRUE and

SpinUpHoldState is not equal to SPIN_UP_NO_HOLD.
   		
  

  

   
17
   
   
 
   
  

  

   
18
   
   
 
   
  

  

   
19
   
   
 
   
  

  

   

LogicalHdValid
   

   
20
   
   
 
   
   
LogicalHdValid, if TRUE, and SpinUpHoldState is not equal to SPIN_UP_NO_HOLD,

indicates that the LogicalHd is valid and specifies the address of the logical

head on which the servo will attempt to synchronize the demodulator and / or

track follow after spinning up.  If LogicalHdValid is FALSE or the SpinUpHoldState

is equal to SPIN_UP_NO_HOLD, the servo will attempt synchronize the demodulator

and / or track follow on the default logical head after spinning up.
   		
  

  

   

LogicalHd
   

   
21
   
   
 
   
   
LogicalHd is the address of the logical head on which the servo will attempt to

synchronize the demodulator and / or track follow after spinning up.  It is only used

when LogicalHdValid is TRUE and SpinUpHoldState is not equal to SPIN_UP_NO_HOLD.
   		
  

  

   

reserved
   

   
22..23
   
   
 
   
   
reserved

 Write Servo RAM At Index


  Description:
    This diagnostic mode function writes the servo memory address specified by the contents
    located at the specified index of the internal servo symbol table.

    WARNING: this function does NOT check whether the contents of the Servo Symbol Table
    located at the specified index is a valid memory location since servo does not make
    this information available to the firmware.

   Name
   Byte
Index		
   Value
   Description

3
   
   
0x00

RegData is the data with which the Power ASIC register was written.

    0x0000 - 0x0FFF: Diagnostic Infrastructure Errors
   ******************************************************************************************

    0x0001: Unsupported Diagnostic Feature
    0x0002: Online Extrinsic Requests are disabled

 Read/Write Status Codes


 0x0 RW_REQUEST_SATISFIED_WITH_RECOVERY - Request was satisfied with error recovery performed
 0x1 RW_REQUEST_SATISFIED - Request was satisfied (no error recovery performed)
 0x2 RW_REQUEST_FAILED -Request was not satisfied


 Read/Write Sense Error Codes


 R/W Sense Error Codes are error codes that R/W reports to its clients.  Although they are
 very similar to traditional SCSI sense codes, there is not a one-to-one correspondence with
 traditional SCSI sense codes.  These R/W Sense Error Codes should be treated and interpreted
 independently from them.

 R/W Sense Error Codes may be reported with one or more bits of their most significant nybble
 set.  These bits are described below:

 Bit 31: Move FRU Flag.

         If this bit is set, it indicates that the least significant byte of the sense code
         should be copied into the additional sense code qualifier when it is translated into
         a SCSI sense code.

 Bit 30: Read/Write Retryable Error Type.

         If this bit is set, it indicates that the condition that caused R/W to report the
         R/W Sense Error Code is retryable.  This gives R/W clients an opportunity perform
         higher level retries.  IMPORTANT!  Please note that R/W Sense Error Codes that are
         reported in a diagnostic environment (e.g. serial port debug statements) should
         never be considered hard errors when this bit is set.

   ***************************************************************************
    Internal x0/00 Errors.
   ***************************************************************************
    0x00000080: RW_NO_ERRORS - No R/W Errors encountered.
    0x00000081: RW_REQUEST_ABORTED - Request failed due to abort of request.

    0x00000083: RW_DATA_SCRUB_SUCCESSFUL - Reallocate Block - Data scrub of the original sector was successful.

 Read/Write Retry Characters

    '*': PATH_ERROR_CHAR - DERP illegal path
    '#': RESET_FIR_RECOV_CHAR - Reset FIR tweak recovery character
    '~': SM_TOLERANCE_RECOV_CHAR - Sync mark tolerance recovery character
    ')': POST_ACQUIRE_RECOV_CHAR - Post acquire recovery character
    '(': TRACKING_PLO_RECOV_CHAR - Tracking PLO tweak recovery character
    '$': TRACKING_PLO_SLIP_RECOV_CHAR - Tracking PLO SLIP tweak recovery character
    ';': DERP_READ_RECOV_CHAR - Data recovery character
    '"': ZGS_VGA_RECOV_CHAR
    '&': ID_SPLASH_RETRY_CHAR - Splash retry char
    '.': DATA_RECOV_CHAR - Data recovery character
    '%': DATA_SCRUB_FIRST_WRITE_1
    '2': DATA_SCRUB_FIRST_WRITE_2
    '1': DATA_SCRUB_SECOND_WRITE
    '1': DATA_SCRUB_READ
    '@': DATA_SCRUB_ATTEMPTS_EXCEEDED
    'a': ACQUIRE_PLO_RECOV_CHAR - Acquire PLO recovery character
    'B': BURNISH_RETRY_CHAR
    'b': FILTER_RECOV_CHAR - Filter tweak recovery character
    'C': CHANNEL_RELOAD_CHAR - Channel Reload recovery
    'c': ECC_OTF_RECOV_CHAR - ECC on-the-fly correction performed character
    'D': RG_DELAY_CHAR - RG Delay
    'D': SWD_DVGAS_RECOV_CHAR
    'd': CLEARANCE_RETRY_CHAR - Clearance value adjusted during recovery
    'E': EP0_RETRY_CHAR
    'e': EP3_RETRY_CHAR
    'F': CLEARANCE_RETRY_CHAR - Clearance value adjusted during recovery
    'F': AGC_RECOV_CHAR - AGC tweak recovery character
    'f': RESET_FIR_RECOV_CHAR - Reset FIR tweak recovery character
    'G': FORCED_NLFR_RECOV_CHAR - Forced NLFR tweak recovery character
    'g': TRACKING_PLO_RECOV_CHAR - Tracking PLO tweak recovery character
    'H': FILTER_RECOV_CHAR - Filter tweak recovery character
    'h': AGC_RECOV_CHAR - AGC tweak recovery character
    'h': LOW_SYNC_MARK_TOL_RECOV_CHAR - Low sync mark tolerance tweak recovery character
    'i': IOEDC_RECOV_CHAR - IOEDC recovery character
    'j': EP2_RETRY_CHAR
    'k': HEATER_CONTROL_FAULT_RECOV_CHAR
    'L': SERVO_FORCE_COAST_RETRY_CHAR
    'M': MR_BIAS_RETRY_CHAR - MR bias tweak retry character
    'm': SM_TOLERANCE_RECOV_CHAR - Sync mark tolerance recovery character
    'N': SECOND_SYNC_RETRY_CHAR
    'P': POST_ACQUIRE_RECOV_CHAR - Post acquire recovery character
    'n': FORCED_NLFR_RECOV_CHAR - Forced NLFR tweak recovery character
    'N': DERP_NEW_SEQ_CHAR - Shows start of new DERP sequence
    'N': FORCED_NEG_SYNC_RETRY_CHAR - Forced Negitive Sync retry char
    'O': OFFSET_ISSUED_CHAR
    'o': OFFSET_RETRY_CHAR
    'P': FORCED_POS_SYNC_RETRY_CHAR - Forced Positive Sync retry char
    'p': ACQUIRE_PLO_RECOV_CHAR - Acquire PLO recovery character
    'p': PFAST_RETRY_CHAR - Power chop/pfast retry character
    'Q': EP1_RETRY_CHAR
    'q': WRITE_SERVO_UNSAFE_RECOV_CHAR - Servo unsafe error recovery character
    'S': SEEK_AWAY_RETRY_CHAR
    's': LARGE_SHOCK_EVENT_RETRY_CHAR - Retry done to recover form a Large Shock Event
    'T': SOFT_EP_RETRY_CHAR
    't': SETUP_TA_MODE_RECOV_CHAR - Setup TA modes Character
    'u': DERP_CHAN_UNTWEAK_CHAR - Channel Untweak
    'V': REV_POL_RETRY_CHAR - Reverse Polarity retry character
    'v': RW_PRINT_RETRY_VIBRATION_DETECTION_WRITE
    'V': RW_PRINT_RETRY_VIBRATION_WRITE
    'U': SWD_FVGAS_RECOV_CHAR - Skip Write Detect recovery characters
    'V': SWD_RVGAS_RECOV_CHAR
    'W': SLIDING_WINDOW_RETRY_CHAR
    'w': WRITE_RECOV_CHAR - Write recovery character
    'Y': PREAMP_UNSAFE_RECOV_CHAR - Preamp unsafe recovery character
    'Z': TRACK_OFFSET_RETRY_CHAR
    'z': ZAP_ENABLE_DISABLE_CHAR - Indicates zap enabled/disabled
    '|': PZT_RECAL_RETRY_CHAR
   


Defined Error Recovery Status Bit Flags

0x0001: BIT 0: RW_RECOVERY_POS_TRK_OFF_APPLIED - Error was recovered w/positive track offset applied.
0x0002: BIT 1: RW_RECOVERY_NEG_TRK_OFF_APPLIED - Error was recovered w/negative track offset applied.
0x0004: BIT 2: RW_RECOVERY_ECC_CORR_APPLIED - Error was recovered w/ECC correction applied.
0x0008: BIT 3: RW_RECOVERY_SYNC_RECOVERY_APPLIED - Error was recovered w/sync mark recovery.
0x0010: BIT 4: RW_RECOVERY_HIDDEN_RETRY_APPLIED - Error was recovered w/hidden retry applied.
0x0020: BIT 5: RW_RECOVERY_GROWN_SERVO_FLAWS_EXIST - Grown servo flaws exist on current track..
0x0040: BIT 6: RW_RECOVERY_SERVO_FLAW_ASSOCIATED - Retried block is associated w/a servo flaw.
0x0080: BIT 7: RW_RECOVERY_NEW_SERVO_FLAWS_DETECTED - New servo flaws detected during recovery.
0x0100: BIT 8: RW_RECOVERY_TIME_EXCEEDED - Recovery time limit was exceeded.
0x0200: BIT 9: RW_RECOVERY_LEVEL_EXCEEDED - Recovery level limit was exceeded.
0x0400: BIT 10: RW_RECOVERY_COUNT_EXCEEDED - Recovery count limit was exceeded.
0x0800: BIT 11: RW_RECOVERED_SEEK_OCCURRED - Recovered seek error occurred.
0x1000: BIT 12: RW_RECOVERY_DID_ECC_NOT_FWEC - When FW Erasure correction was applied, normal ECC was actually used
                                               this will be set along with RW_RECOVERY_ECC_CORR_APPLIED
0x2000: BIT 13: BIPS_BUFFER_XOR_RECOVERY_APPLIED - Error was recovered w/BIPS recovery applied.
0x4000: BIT 14: RW_READ_CONTINUOUS_EDAC_HU_ERR_OCCURRED - EDAC HU error occurred in read continuous transfer.
0x8000: BIT 15: RW_APPROACHING_RECOVERY_TIME_LIMIT - When R/W has detected the recovery time limit is approaching,
                                                     this bit will be set along with RW_RECOVERY_TIME_EXCEEDED
0x10000: BIT 16: RW_RECOVERY_SERV_APPLIED - Error was recovered w/SERV recovery applied.


Flash LED Codes


Codes marked (++) are duplicated in sys.i for assembly language wrappers.
Codes marked (**) are converted to FRU codes for reporting in sense data.

0x00 INVALID_FLASH_LED_CODE            00000000 (**) Invalid flash code
0x08 MICRO_FAIL                        00001000 (++) ARM failure, Unexpected FIQ interrupt
0x0B BUFFER_FAIL                       00001011 (++) DRAM failed powerup or WRAM fail.
0x0C SCC_FAIL                          00001100 (**) Controller failed power up diagnostics
0x0D CTLR_VERSION_FAIL                 00001101 Controller not compatible with firmware
0x0E UNOPCODE_OCCUR                    00001110 (**) Unimplemented Opcode interrupt

0x10 XOR_FAIL                          00010000 (**) XOR power up test failed (tested even on non-XOR code)
0x12 PROG_ERR_EVEN                     00010010 EEPROM verify error, even byte
0x13 ERASE_ERR_EVEN                    00010011 EEPROM erase error, even byte
0x14 DL_TPM_FAIL_0                     00010100 TPM could not program EEPROMs
0x15 DL_TPM_FAIL_1                     00010101 TPM could not program EEPROMs
0x16 DL_TPM_FAIL_2                     00010110 TPM could not program EEPROMs
0x17 DL_TPM_FAIL_3                     00010111 TPM could not program EEPROMs
0x18 DL_TPM_FAIL_4                     00011000 TPM could not program EEPROMs
0x19 DL_TPM_FAIL_5                     00011001 TPM could not program EEPROMs
0x1A DL_TPM_FAIL_6                     00011010 TPM could not program EEPROMs
0x1B DL_TPM_FAIL_7                     00011011 TPM could not program EEPROMs
0x1C DL_TPM_FAIL_8                     00011100 TPM could not program EEPROMs
0x1D DWNLD_VFLT                        00011101 Download voltage fault

0x40 ALU_BUFPE_FAIL                    01000000 ALU buffer parity error
0x42 ERROR_INJECTION_ASSERT_CODE       01000010 Assert code reported when an assert event is triggered
                                                by error injection and no assert code has been given.
0x44 BUF_CFG_FAIL                      01000100 DRAM configuration process failed
0x45 FDE_BUSPARITY_ERR                 01000101
0x47 PREFETCH_VEC                      01000111 (++) (**) Prefetch abort exception (intvect.a)
0x47 SP_FAIL                           01000111 (**) Stack pointer out of range
0x4C READ_CHIP_ERR                     01001100 (**) Error in writing to read chip
0x4D IER_STACK_OVFL                    01001101 (**) IER stack overflow
0x4E IER_STACK_UNFL                    01001110 (**) IER stack underflow
0x4F IER_STACK_ERR                     01001111 (**) stack not empty on entry to sleep

0x55 IRAW_HAD_IOEDC_ERROR              01010101
0x5f IRAW_HAD_MISCOMPARE               01011111

0x67 UNDEFINED_INSTRUCTION             01100111, (++) Undefined opcode exception (intvect.a)

0x77 LOG_SAVE_FAIL                     01110111, (**) Log save data has exceeded the maximum allowable size

0x80 PORT_FAIL                         10000000, (**) Ports A & B failed power up diags
0x81 NO_BACKPLANE_DATA_RATE            10000001, (**) Can't find back plane data rate
0x81 DATA_RATE_NOT_FOUND               10000001, Can't find back plane data rate

0x90 CITCM_UNRECOVERABLE_ERROR         10010000, Controller I-TCM unrecoverable error
0x91 CDTCM_UNRECOVERABLE_ERROR         10010001, Controller D-TCM unrecoverable error
0x92 SITCM_UNRECOVERABLE_ERROR         10010010, Servo I-TCM unrecoverable error
0x93 SDTCM_UNRECOVERABLE_ERROR         10010011, Servo D-TCM unrecoverable error
0x9D TCM_CRC_FAIL                      10011101, (**) TCM CRC result is non-zero

0xC4 DRAM_INTEGRITY_FAILURE            11000100, (**) DRAM was detected to be corrupt on a write
0xCC ASSERT_FLASH_CODE                 11001100, (++) Assert failure
0xCD ENSURE_FLASH_CODE                 11001101, (++) Ensure failure
0xCE REQUIRE_FLASH_CODE                11001110, (++) Require failure

0xD1 SCSI_UNEXP_INT                    11010001, (**) Unexpected SCSI interrupt
0xD2 SCSI_TIMEOUT_FLASH_CODE           11010010, (++) SCSI timeout
0xD3 ILLEGAL_STATUS_CODE_FLASH_CODE    11010011, (++) Illegal status code
0xD4 SCSI_UNDER_OVER_RUN_OCCURED       11010100, SCSI Hardware was Overrun or Underun by the host
0xD5 UNEXPECTED_STATUS_CODE            11010101, Unexpected status code from the sequencer
0xDD DIVBY0_FAIL                       11011101, (++) (**) Divide by zero interrupt, SWI range error

0xEE ABORT_FAIL                        11101110, (**) Data abort exception (intvect.a)

0xF1 CTLR_NUKED_BY_FDE                 11110001, FDE Nuke the chip bit set, data transfers not allowed
0xF4 FLASH_IOEDC_PARITY_ERROR          11110100, (**) temporarily flash on IOEDC_PARITY_ERROR
